  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_96b15958-476a-42b5-8e51-360a44052b3d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText7691129614384170210" style="display:none">By scheming and theft, the Thief of Eddis has become King of Attolia. Eugenides wanted the queen, not the crown, but he finds himself trapped in a web of his own making.<br /><br />Then he drags a naive young guard into the center of the political maelstrom. Poor Costis knows he is the victim of the king's caprice, but his contempt for Eugenides slowly turns to grudging respect. Though struggling against his fate, the newly crowned king is much more than he appears. Soon the corrupt Attolian court will learn that its subtle and dangerous intrigue is no match for Eugenides.</span>

I like the writing style very much. There is some swearing, but intimacy is only assumed between husband and wife and not shown. <span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I agree with the others. You will miss a great deal if you read this book without reading the previous books in the series. Also, I can't think of any<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I agree with the others. You will miss a great deal if you read this book without reading the previous books in the series. Also, I can't think of any reason you would want to. The books are *SO* good, all of them. Any reason you have for reading this book applies to the rest of the series.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_230907474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230907474" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230907474?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230907474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9812652576122899190"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>It's weird how I find the most difficult books to review are those that I knew were going to be amazing... and yep, this was amazing! I mean, what do you say that actually means anything? I could ramble on about <i>fantastic</i> writing, <i>brilliant</i> characters, <i>excellent</i> plot, this would all be true but the words are so empty and don't convey what I love about this series.<br/><br/>They don't say how this intricate fantasy world pulls you in with it's politics, it's culture and it's superstitions. It's like th</span>
  <span id="freeText9812652576122899190" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It's weird how I find the most difficult books to review are those that I knew were going to be amazing... and yep, this was amazing! I mean, what do you say that actually means anything? I could ramble on about <i>fantastic</i> writing, <i>brilliant</i> characters, <i>excellent</i> plot, this would all be true but the words are so empty and don't convey what I love about this series.<br><br>They don't say how this intricate fantasy world pulls you in with it's politics, it's culture and it's superstitions. It's like the excitement of walking through a wardrobe into the strange land of Narnia and not knowing what's around every corner, but needing to find out. There is no map provided in these books (at least not in my editions) but the parts of the world that we have explored so far are completely imaginable to me. I can imagine Attolia by the coast and picture the mountains running through this world that forge geographical, political and cultural boundaries. Am I starting to waffle? That's because I am in love with this series; is this how Romeo felt? "Did my heart love till now? Forswear it, sight! For I ne'er saw true beauty till this night." Okay, all right, I'm stopping before it gets even weirder.<br><br>I don't understand how so many authors can write in 1st person and still fail to create characters that interest me as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> does so easily in her 3rd person perspective. Perhaps it is that she only reveals what is absolutely necessary and the characters we think we know can so easily surprise us. This book is told from the point of view of Costis (an Attolian soldier) who is assigned to be the King's lieutenant and witnesses much of the goings on around the palace. I'm starting to think that this is ultimately the more effective way to tell a story. Well, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights" title="Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Wuthering Heights</a> was told entirely from the point of view of secondary characters, for one!<br><br>The story was excellent, I loved visiting Eugenides again and seeing how far he has come and how much he is still the same little devil we met in book one. This is a novel full of palace politics, new friendships, conspiracies, assassins and a dash of romance. I wasn't sure how the relationship between the new King and the Queen of Attolia would work out, but Turner handled it perfectly and the chemistry between two such unlikely companions was very exciting to read.<br><br>Oh and, of course, this is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> so you can be sure that nothing is as it seems...<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9812652576122899190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2376881446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376881446" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2376881446?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062642981" href="/book/show/30363361-the-king-of-attolia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-audiobook">x-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376881446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16415249992657030459"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Are you badly hurt?”<br/>“Hideously,” said the king, without sounding injured at all. “I am disemboweled. My insides may in an instant become my outsides as I stand here before you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Attolis, the new king of Attolia, is a pawn. He is lazy, unloved by his wife, and there to be a victim, unaware of the political machinations of his court. At least, that’s what his guard thinks of him; they love their queen, of course, but do not love their king. This includes Costis, his newly appointed gua</span>
  <span id="freeText16415249992657030459" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Are you badly hurt?”<br />“Hideously,” said the king, without sounding injured at all. “I am disemboweled. My insides may in an instant become my outsides as I stand here before you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Attolis, the new king of Attolia, is a pawn. He is lazy, unloved by his wife, and there to be a victim, unaware of the political machinations of his court. At least, that’s what his guard thinks of him; they love their queen, of course, but do not love their king. This includes Costis, his newly appointed guard, who hates him. With a clever point of view shift to a new character, this book is a clever and eerie ride.<br /><br />This series feels so classic, like something everyone would’ve been obsessed with ten years ago. I hope people will still obssess over it now. <br /><br />So what do people always praise about this series? Because item #1 is the plotting, and item #2 is the character work. I second <i>both</i>. <br /><br />I’ve been thinking a lot about why the plotting of this series is so great, and it’s because Megan Whalen Turner is so good at <b>planting and payoff.</b> If a plot element shows up in the beginning of the book, it will be become a part of the book further on; within the world, with political elements, with character elements. Element after element is used for plot twists and it is always <i>so satisfying</i> and compelling.<br /><br />And perhaps even more importantly, the character work here is fucking incredible. Gen is a fantastic mastermind. Costis is an impressively likable character, especially as he’s just shown up. Gen and Irene are one of the most endearing couples I have ever read about. Also, I absolutely love and <i>adore</i> the dialogue. It’s glorious and adds so much to these characters.<br /><br />So why only four stars? You know, this has gotten the hype of being the best book in this series, and I have to admit, I’m not sure it lived up to that. One of my absolute favorite parts of <a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> was the development of Irene; her slow character arc, the growing relationship between her and Gen. This book… lacked Irene. Okay, she’s there plenty, but I LOVE her and she was not in this book enough. Costis is a really interesting character and I really loved the growing relationship between him and Gen, but I admit, I was disappointed by the overall smaller scale of the plot twists and the action. <br /><br />I do really like that this series is becoming primarily the story of <b>
  <u>small but powerful players within a very large world,</u>
</b> but the shift was surprising, especially as the narrator, Costis, drives very little of the plot. It’s an interesting plot device, but as a result, I found myself losing focus on action within the middle. But this worked pretty well, because we’re so invested in the characters involved in the action. <br /><br />And when it comes down to it, I really enjoyed this. It’s such a fun classic fantasy; I feel reminded of old Kristin Cashore and Tamora Pierce in the <i>best</i> way. It is a fantastic read and I cannot wait to get to the next book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>here are my other series thoughts:</i>
</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995733992" rel="nofollow noopener">book one</a> - ★★★☆☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030955705" rel="nofollow noopener">book two</a> - ★★★★★<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376881446" rel="nofollow noopener">book three</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2467555040" rel="nofollow noopener">book four</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484905696" rel="nofollow noopener">book five</a> - ★★★★★<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2461451115" rel="nofollow noopener">book six</a> - TBD<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

<div id="review_87920720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87920720" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87920720?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060835798" href="/book/show/448872.The_King_of_Attolia">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Kristin Cashore, Robin McKinley</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mythopoeic">mythopoeic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87920720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5861948658770970736">With this book Megan Whalen Turner has cemented herself as one of my all-time favorite writers. I absolutely loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87920704' rel='nofollow noopener'>"The Queen of Attolia"</a> and "The King of Attolia" is a remarkable follow-up.<br/><br/>Eugenides, the famous Thief of Eddis, is now the King of Attolia. He is married to the woman he loves but he doesn't enjoy the power that comes with it. Gen is despised by Attolians, they think him a lazy fool and a treacherous abuser of their Queen. But of course, things are not at all what they seem to be..</span>
  <span id="freeText5861948658770970736" style="display:none">With this book Megan Whalen Turner has cemented herself as one of my all-time favorite writers. I absolutely loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87920704" rel="nofollow noopener">"The Queen of Attolia"</a> and "The King of Attolia" is a remarkable follow-up.<br /><br />Eugenides, the famous Thief of Eddis, is now the King of Attolia. He is married to the woman he loves but he doesn't enjoy the power that comes with it. Gen is despised by Attolians, they think him a lazy fool and a treacherous abuser of their Queen. But of course, things are not at all what they seem to be...<br /><br />The book is almost entirely written from the POV of Costis, an ordinary guard who at the opening of the book physically assaults the King. Instead of being executed, Costis is pardoned by Eugenides and soon even becomes one of his closest attendants and a center of various court intrigues. Slowly Costis, and we together with him, starts learning who his new King really is, the nature of Gen's relationship with his Queen and his schemes that are intended to reshape the landscape of Attolian politics.<br /><br />As Turner's previous book, "The King of Attolia" is filled with political intrigues and power play, this time almost exclusively within the Attolian court. Another excellent addition - Turner's examination of royal power and the nature of loyalty to the superiors - a very skillful and clever touch. The characters (I am mostly talking about Gen and Irene) still remain almost anonymous to us (as they are to Attolians), the narration is not overburdened with their emotional turmoils, but whatever we get a glimpse of - for instance, Gen's complicated relationship with his wife (we all know <i>their</i> history and they both are not quite over it) - is touching and deep. <br /><br />What else can I say? "The King of Attolia" is another masterful novel by Megan Whalen Turner. I expect I will enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87920728" rel="nofollow noopener">"A Conspiracy of Kings"</a> just as much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5861948658770970736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_47728324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47728324" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50378-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510342996p2/50378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47728324?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=belovedbookshelf">belovedbookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=e-p-i-c">e-p-i-c</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47728324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1574290193521713104">If I tell you that each book in this series just gets more and more exceptional, will you believe me? Or will you believe that I, like Eugenides, am simply telling you a version of the truth to get you to do what I want you to do? (In this case, to get you to read these books yesterday). Both things are true, by the way. <i>The King of Attolia</i> <b>is</b> even better than its predecessor and I will tell you <b>anything</b> to get you to read these books. Yesterday. Plus, check out my favorite cover of the three. L</span>
  <span id="freeText1574290193521713104" style="display:none">If I tell you that each book in this series just gets more and more exceptional, will you believe me? Or will you believe that I, like Eugenides, am simply telling you a version of the truth to get you to do what I want you to do? (In this case, to get you to read these books yesterday). Both things are true, by the way. <i>The King of Attolia</i> <b>is</b> even better than its predecessor and I will tell you <b>anything</b> to get you to read these books. Yesterday. Plus, check out my favorite cover of the three. Look at the feather scar on his cheek. Her hand on his shoulder. His grip on the sword. So awesome.<br /><br />Eugenides has just embarked upon his self-imposed life of exile in Attolia. And to any and all onlookers, he is ill at ease in his new home. The queen appears to despise him, the court thinks him an idiot of epic proportions, and the guard are ready to murder him on their queen's behalf. The story follows a young lieutenant named Costis who is having a shockingly bad day. In a fit of righteous indignation, he hauled off and punched the king in the face in front of several witnesses, including the captain of the guard. Certain he will hang in the morning, Costis is shocked and discomfited to find himself assigned to be the king's personal assistant. Forced to serve the man he hates, Costis soon finds himself on the receiving end of a most unorthodox education of a lifetime. Through his eyes, the reader gets an intimate, exquisitely poignant look at the relationship between the King and the Queen of Attolia. <br /><br />This third installment is the big payoff in many ways. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19063.The_Book_Thief" title="The Book Thief by Markus Zusak" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> set up the key characters, briefly sketching out their backgrounds and motivations--all against a background of a grand quest--and it did it with humor and style. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__Eugenides__Book_2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (Eugenides, Book 2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> delved into the complicated psyches of the two main players, word by artfully chosen word, making your heart ache for them, ensuring you fall in love with them. <i>The King of Attolia</i> cements the whole gorgeous package. This is where Eugenides comes into his own. This is where you realize he's smarter than you. And so is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a>. And you wouldn't have it any other way. This book is the real deal. Every scene is choice. Every sarcastic exchange. Every vicious riposte. Every hidden glance. It's a rereader's paradise and, as Oscar Wilde said, "If one cannot enjoy reading a book over and over again, there is no use in reading it at all." <i>The King of Attolia</i> is so worth it. I can already tell I will be reading about these characters for the rest of my life. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1574290193521713104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1337482545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1337482545" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1337482545?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1337482545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6992964099572619527">Buddy Read with some series fanatics at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books & Baubles</a> <br/><br/>This series isn’t your typical sort of fantasy. Most of the book is more intellectual than actionable in that I spent most of the time trying to figure out the subtle interactions between Eugenides and the Queen of Attolia.<br/><br/>After a few books shown from the PoVs of Eudenidies and The Queens it was interesting that most of this book was shown from the perspective of Costis a member of the Attolian guard. At first I didn’t really unders</span>
  <span id="freeText6992964099572619527" style="display:none">Buddy Read with some series fanatics at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</a> <br /><br />This series isn’t your typical sort of fantasy. Most of the book is more intellectual than actionable in that I spent most of the time trying to figure out the subtle interactions between Eugenides and the Queen of Attolia.<br /><br />After a few books shown from the PoVs of Eudenidies and The Queens it was interesting that most of this book was shown from the perspective of Costis a member of the Attolian guard. At first I didn’t really understand what the author was doing, but then it made perfect sense. It was a much more interesting story to see how everyone else in Attolia perceived Gen and try to figure out what he was really up to. If we got the story from his perspective then the mystery of it wouldn’t have been half as entertaining. I almost feel bad for Costis caught in whatever game Gen is playing.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Don’t hang Teleus. But I don’t see how you can hang Costis if you won’t hang his superior officer.” <br />The queen turned back to face him. <br />“I could hang you,” she said. <br />Eugenides looked up at her. “You missed your chance for that,” he said. <br />The queen lifted a hand to briefly cover her eyes. “It is remarkable how you cloud my otherwise clear vision,” she said. “What is it you propose?” <br />“I propose that you let me trade him to Teleus. His life in return for Teleus’s good behavior.”</i>
</blockquote><br />AND LET THE GAMES BEGIN…..The people of Attolia have made sure that Gen does not feel the least bit welcome in their country. Most of the time they like to refer to him as a <i>jumped-up barbarian goatfoot</i> and play little vengeful tricks on him in order to chip away at his resolve and respect. It was so weird to see what they thought of him since we know how deadly he truly is.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> The gods above knew that the king could be laid out by a toddler with a toasting fork. What hope had he against an assassin, trained as a sword is sharpened, honed to one purpose, to murder?</i>
</blockquote><br />I really enjoyed trying to figure out myself what game he was playing and why he was pretending to be so much less than he was. While I was certain there was something up I struggled to put the clues together. Everyone thought that they were getting the best of Eugenides, when he was really maneuvering them to move to the steps of the dance he set in motion. <br /><br />We get little glimpses of Gen and the Queen together and it made it all the more special to also see those through Costis’s eyes. There aren’t a lot of them as this is not a romance per say but the moments we get really are pretty beautiful and spectacular because there aren’t a lot of them.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Tell me you won’t cut out my lying tongue, tell me you won’t blind me, you won’t drive red-hot wires into my ears.” <br />After one moment of gripped immobility, the queen bent to kiss the king lightly on one closed eyelid, then on the other. She said, “I love your eyes.” She kissed him on either cheek, near the small lobe of his ear. “I love your ears, and I love”—she paused as she kissed him gently on the lips—“every single one of your ridiculous lies.”</i>
</blockquote><br />There are a few moments of action in the book. But for the most part it is a political maneuvering conspiracy and most of the fun was in the revelation of clues and the big reveal of why Eugenides would put up with so much for so long. There was a great sword fight towards the end and I enjoyed the reason behind it and why it finally happened. It was great to see Gen finally figure out his place in Attolia and claim it in true Thief fashion.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6992964099572619527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3565065805" />

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3565065805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10007139889056578437"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I'm going to save you a bunch of time and heartbreak, and tell you something I wish someone had told me before I was seduced by the sea of glowing four- and five-star reviews for this book: If you liked the first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3539488197' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE THIEF</a>, the sequel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3547726763' rel='nofollow noopener'>QUEEN OF ATTOLIA</a>, is going to depress and anger you, and KING OF ATTOLIA is going to bore and frustrate you. There, I said it.<br/><br/><br/><br/>THE THIEF was one of my childhood favorites. I read it in middle school a</span>
  <span id="freeText10007139889056578437" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I'm going to save you a bunch of time and heartbreak, and tell you something I wish someone had told me before I was seduced by the sea of glowing four- and five-star reviews for this book: If you liked the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3539488197" rel="nofollow noopener">THE THIEF</a>, the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3547726763" rel="nofollow noopener">QUEEN OF ATTOLIA</a>, is going to depress and anger you, and KING OF ATTOLIA is going to bore and frustrate you. There, I said it.<br><br><br><br>THE THIEF was one of my childhood favorites. I read it in middle school and really enjoyed it-- it stayed on my childhood bookshelf for <i>years</i> before I finally got rid of it in favor of other books, but it was a story I never forgot. All of these stories are set in a fantasy world inspired by Ancient Greece, where the gods interact with and look over their charges, but tend to take a light hand in favor of letting the mortals figure out things for themselves-- even at the cost of their suffering (read: see QUEEN OF ATTOLIA).<br><br><br><br>THE THIEF is narrated in first person and I <i>loved </i>Gen's voice, which made QUEEN OF ATTOLIA somewhat of a disappointment because it's narrated in third person-- and Megan Whalen Turner decides to torture the everloving hell out of her poor character, in a way that wouldn't have felt out of place in a <i>Game of Thrones </i>episode. I was honestly shocked, because even though there is violence and intrigue in the first book, it's pretty mild, whereas tonally and contextually, the sequel seems much older in terms of the age group it's targeting. This is not really made clear, and thank goodness somebody warned me.<br><br><br><br>In KING OF ATTOLIA, the reader is removed yet another step from Gen. Now the narration (still in third person, blast it) is from a guard named Costis, who is loyal to the queen of Attolia but ends up serving the king by marriage. Costis has a lot of scorn for the king at first and undermines him at every turn with resentment. But gradually, he comes to realize that the king isn't the usurping fool he imagined; in fact, he might be worse-- a blend of compassion and danger that makes him infinitely lethal and foolish to underestimate. That is really the only saving grace of this book-- the twists. There's always a great twist at the end of one of these books that just completely turns everything on its head.<br><br><br><br>So, I'm a little torn on what to read this book. It's filled with way too many characters I didn't care about (including the narrator), and takes way too long to get where it's going. Towards the 55% mark, it picks up-- <i>finally</i>-- and the payoff is good but isn't really worth the slog. Plus, I freaking <i>hate </i>the Queen of Attolia still and I think it's quite disgusting how the ship between her and Gen is forced in. I don't buy them as a couple anymore than I did Rhysand and Feyre from the ACoTaR series. I'm sorry, but you can't just ret-con a bunch of abuse and problematic behavior for the sake of your ships and your plot contrivances. I won't buy it, and it's lazy as all get out, and it makes me write reviews with a frown.<br><br><br><br>If I hadn't already bought the next two books in the series, I would have quit here. But apparently Sophos is in the next book and I like him, so hopefully this means Costis will be left in the dust.<br><br><br><br>P.S. Hugs and smiles to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/19869239-erika-owlwaysreading" rel="nofollow noopener">Erika</a> for BR-ing this series with me. Her reaction to the events in QUEEN OF ATTOLIA made me feel like I was slightly less delusional and I'm so grateful for that. <br><br><br><br>2.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="10007139889056578437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1475357099" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1475357099" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49847688-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502386968p2/49847688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1475357099?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/49847688-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49847688-emily?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49847688-emily?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49847688-emily?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1475357099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18357156304808978355">I honestly think these books should be required reading for any aspiring fantasy author. And more than a few published fantasy authors. It's just a <i>
  <b>masterclass</b>
</i> in fantastical storytelling.<br/><br/>This is the third in the Queen's Thief series, and so far it's the strongest. The story is primarily told from the perspective of Costis, an Attolian soldier. In less skilled hands, this switch in perspective could have been disastrous. Instead, in Whalen Turner's more than capable hands, it reinvigorates a</span>
  <span id="freeText18357156304808978355" style="display:none">I honestly think these books should be required reading for any aspiring fantasy author. And more than a few published fantasy authors. It's just a <i>
  <b>masterclass</b>
</i> in fantastical storytelling.<br /><br />This is the third in the Queen's Thief series, and so far it's the strongest. The story is primarily told from the perspective of Costis, an Attolian soldier. In less skilled hands, this switch in perspective could have been disastrous. Instead, in Whalen Turner's more than capable hands, it reinvigorates a series that I didn't even think <i>needed</i> reinvigorating!<br /><br />Looking back at the series as a whole, I get why Whalen Turner made the choice to distance the reader from Eugenides, who we've followed closely through two previous books. In this installment, Gen feels isolated and alienated. The perspective switch is a smart way to mirror these feelings in the reader without turning them off the book, without making them feel alienated from the book <i>
  <b>itself</b>
</i>. It's just... So good. <br /><br />And by choosing Costis as our new perspective, Whalen Turner simultaneously expands the world and adds nuance and complexity to the plot. The previous books were focused on the upper echelons of society--kings and queens, courtiers and court advisors. Costis is a solider, and seeing the more intimate details of his world in turn expands the greater world of the Queen's Thief series.<br /><br />It also adds nuance to what could have easily become a standard formula for Whalen Turner. We know Gen, we love Gen, and it is incredibly fun watching him scheme his way to success. In book two, <i>The Queen's Thief</i>, Whalen Turner subverts our expectations by having Gen fail utterly, fail <b>spectacularly</b>. But how could she possibly do that again in book three? <br /><br />Enter Costis. By giving the Attolian people a stand-in perspective, suddenly the Attolians aren't just simple antagonists to stand in opposition to Gen. We see their perspective, understand their hesitations and even hatred for Gen. It makes Gen's new challenges all the more complicated, and the story all the more compelling.<br /><br />I could go on, and on, and on, about these books. The short of it? They are absolutely brilliant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18357156304808978355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2788302067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2788302067" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2788302067?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2788302067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10924562435311676461">This third instalment in Megan Whalen Turner's <i>The Queen's Thief</i> series is easily the best yet. I feel like this series is getting better and better as it progresses as Turner seems to have figured out what works and what does not and makes the correct adjustments. This series is an old school coming of age YA fantasy story in many ways but what sets it apart is that the focus tends to be on intrigue and character development rather than flashy action scenes. It also helps that Turner is a cleve</span>
  <span id="freeText10924562435311676461" style="display:none">This third instalment in Megan Whalen Turner's <i>The Queen's Thief</i> series is easily the best yet. I feel like this series is getting better and better as it progresses as Turner seems to have figured out what works and what does not and makes the correct adjustments. This series is an old school coming of age YA fantasy story in many ways but what sets it apart is that the focus tends to be on intrigue and character development rather than flashy action scenes. It also helps that Turner is a clever writer. Scenes that at first glance tend to feel a little throwaway often tend to turn out to be significant set up work for later happenings in the story. It leaves the reader feeling like Turner had the story planned from start to finish and that there is very little waste and padding. The world itself was heavily inspired by Greek mythology.<br /><br />The story in this one pretty much picked up from where the last book ended. Eugenides is now the King of Attolia. The problem is it is a title and role he never really wanted even if he does recognize the necessity of it and the people of Attolia have good reason to resent him. What we got was a story with a heavy focus on character development and court intrigue. I felt like Turner nailed both so I found this to be a super engaging tale from start to finish. <br /><br />Structurally I feel like Turner did a lot of clever things that made this story the best in the series so far. The scope was very tight with pretty much all of the action taking place in the palace in Attolia and pretty much all the major characters in the story being members of the Attolian court. There was much less of an epic feel to this instalment of the series than there was in the previous books but surprisingly this turned out to be an advantage as the characters and the court intrigue benefited from being the sole focus of the story. The other really clever thing Turner did in this one was switch the focus away from Gen and Attolia. The pair were still the main characters and the stars of the book but the fact that we saw them from the eyes of Costis, a young Attolian guard, and a few other servants in the court was a master-stroke. It left the motivations of Gen and Attolia a bit of a mystery and also gave us the chance to see both characters from a different perspective and I felt like that really enriched the story and gave it extra depth. <br /><br />All in all I really enjoyed The King of Attolia and hope the rest of the series delivers this quality of storytelling. <br /><br />Rating: 4.5 stars. I'm rounding down to 4 stars here on Goodreads but that is mostly because I've been picky lately!<br /><br />Audio Note: Jeff Woodman is a fantastic narrator. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10924562435311676461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2788302067">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1030290587" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1030290587" />
    <a title="jade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21073355-jade"><img alt="jade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381337827p2/21073355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1030290587?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jade" href="/user/show/21073355-jade">jade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21073355-jade?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1030290587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17902488878577829376">An awesome, awesome book! <br/><br/>Sweet revenge. When you have a protagonist so much superior mentally and physically than anyone else, yet was taken as a fool and belittled by everyone, it was the COOLEST thing to see him finally reveal his true self, making everyone realize they'd been played all along. Turner was a genius. Her intelligence and imagination made Eugenides a truly brilliant character. <i>"...if Attolia could look like a queen, then Eugenides was like a god revealed...".</i> Furthermore, Turner</span>
  <span id="freeText17902488878577829376" style="display:none">An awesome, awesome book! <br /><br />Sweet revenge. When you have a protagonist so much superior mentally and physically than anyone else, yet was taken as a fool and belittled by everyone, it was the COOLEST thing to see him finally reveal his true self, making everyone realize they'd been played all along. Turner was a genius. Her intelligence and imagination made Eugenides a truly brilliant character. <i>"...if Attolia could look like a queen, then Eugenides was like a god revealed...".</i> Furthermore, Turner made the story that much more interesting by telling it from a third party point of view. The illusion and misconception at the beginning; the subsequent intrigues; and finally the awe, everything was revealed gradually. I was giddy with anticipation reading and guessing Eugenides's maneuvers. I'd had such negative feeling about cutting off Eugenides's hand in the last book that I didn't believe the series and the romantic relationship could recover from that. However, in this book, everything made sense, their relationship flourished. I actually felt Eugenides's losing one hand was essential to the story's perfection. Not many authors could've pulled this off and Turner did it beautifully.<br /><br />Last but not least, the book is a perfect example of "show, not tell". Nothing was told outright to the readers, everything was observed through other people's eye, yet we still got a clear picture of the characters and felt close to them. It was in turn heartwarming, sweet, and heartbreaking, while the story always absorbing. <br /><br />A solid, deserving 5-star.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17902488878577829376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_15144368" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15144368" />
    <a title="Claire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/836167-claire"><img alt="Claire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554950717p2/836167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15144368?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire" href="/user/show/836167-claire">Claire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=long-ago-far-away-fantasy">long-ago-far-away-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=want-to-own">want-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=high-younger-readers">high-younger-readers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=love-love-love">love-love-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=totally-satisfying">totally-satisfying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/836167-claire?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15144368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17248638402751637809">I'm not a mystery reader, and I've never fully appreciated whodunits, so by rights I should have been irritated with the Attolia books rather than enthralled by them. Unguessable twists and turns are the hallmark of the series: the reader can't possible figure out exactly what is going on because we don't have the information necessary, but we're haunted by the certainty that <i>something</i> more is going on than what the other, non-trickster characters are seeing. This was a sick-day reread for me, a</span>
  <span id="freeText17248638402751637809" style="display:none">I'm not a mystery reader, and I've never fully appreciated whodunits, so by rights I should have been irritated with the Attolia books rather than enthralled by them. Unguessable twists and turns are the hallmark of the series: the reader can't possible figure out exactly what is going on because we don't have the information necessary, but we're haunted by the certainty that <i>something</i> more is going on than what the other, non-trickster characters are seeing. This was a sick-day reread for me, and I was just as captured by it this time, even knowing the upcoming twists (those that I could remember, anyway). <br /><br />Eugenides, the Thief of Eddis, has acceded to the throne of Attolia. He sleeps through official meetings, plays the fool, and generally convinces his attendants, Guard, and other members of the court that he is either weak or a buffoon. Most of the narrative is from the perspective of Costis, an honorable guard who's fallen into the unenviable role of being Gen's lackey. He's not the brightest, and his opinion of Gen is nearly as contemptuous as everyone else's, at least in the beginning. What makes the book interesting is that the reader knows better. <br /><br /><u>The King of Attolia</u> is, IMO, the absolute best of the three books. What makes it so excellent is that Megan Whalen Turner's sleight-of-hand with the plot mirrors the complexity of the relationship between the new King and the Queen. Even through the cloudiness and uncertainty of the plot, there are glimpses of powerful emotion that kept me hanging on to every word and possible clue. The backstory of their relationship -- the Queen's torture of Gen, the uncertain coercion of their marriage -- plays a huge role, coloring every important element of the story. <br /><br />There's been a lot of discussion about whether the narrative gaps in this book are an intentional plot tool or due to its being a sequel. Many people believe it could stand alone. I think it's clear that the narrative gaps are a tool, but I think the whole emotional web that gives the book such intriguing weight is dependent on the <u>The Queen of Attolia</u>. (I think <u>The Thief</u> serves primarily to show that Gen is more than he appears.) <br /><br />I heard a rumor that a fourth book is on its way, and as there were several Sounis-related loose ends that weren't tied up in this book, I'm hopeful! These keep getting better and better. Please write more!<br /><br />Feb 2020 update: reread again, on audio this time, and the narrator is not only outstanding but the way the audiobook version forces me to slow down and catch every detail is *chef's kiss*. My favorite, I think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17248638402751637809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Gen, Gen, Gen, only the most fully awesome, amazing, charming, sneaky little devil that you can't help but love.   <span id="freeText217790955410599990" style="display:none"><br>Sometimes I just can't even with this series. Gen, Gen, Gen, only the most fully awesome, amazing, charming, sneaky little devil that you can't help but love. (That love that borders on if you were a real person, we would be total besties except only in my mind cause you're way too awesome to hang out with the likes of me. Everything about this is wonderful.<br><br>I had some trepidations about this one (as did quite a few others). I mean, Costis?? NOT Gen's POV?? What is this trickery? <div id="review_732864909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732864909" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/732864909?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer732864909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7607772380546941410">This is my favorite book in one of my favorite fantasy series. It starts out a little bit slow, although it's fun watching for all the clues in the text that I missed the first time I read it. But the second half of this book: it is completely made of awesome. I love every single page of it.<br/><br/>Full review to come, after it's posted on <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com'>www.fantasyliterature.com</a>.<br/><br/>July 2015 reread with the <i>Buddies Books and Baubles</i> group.<br/><br/><b>Prior review:</b><br/>This book is just so brilliant and well plotted. I've noticed that of</span>
  <span id="freeText7607772380546941410" style="display:none">This is my favorite book in one of my favorite fantasy series. It starts out a little bit slow, although it's fun watching for all the clues in the text that I missed the first time I read it. But the second half of this book: it is completely made of awesome. I love every single page of it.<br /><br />Full review to come, after it's posted on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com">www.fantasyliterature.com</a>.<br /><br />July 2015 reread with the <i>Buddies Books and Baubles</i> group.<br /><br /><b>Prior review:</b><br />This book is just so brilliant and well plotted. I've noticed that of all the books on my "Favorites" list, this one has the highest overall average rating, and it's for a very good reason. I can't think of anyone I know who wouldn't enjoy this book and its plot twists.<br /><br />Presumably if you're reading this review you've already read (or are thinking of reading) the first book in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a>, which is also a wonderful book, though I found it a little slower than this one. You really do need to read <i>The Thief</i> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> to understand and appreciate <i>The King of Attolia</i>, though. Personally I didn't like the 2nd book in the series (or the 4th, for that matter) nearly as well as the 1st and 3rd, but they're all worthy books. So go plow through the 2nd book, if only so you can get to this 3rd one in the series. It should not be missed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7607772380546941410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2270271924" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2270271924" />
    <a title="Helen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33424987-helen"><img alt="Helen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523656338p2/33424987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2270271924?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen" href="/user/show/33424987-helen">Helen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33424987-helen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2270271924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11553174326446101547"><b>2.5 STARS</b><br/><br/>What the hell happened here? This was supposed to become one of my favourite series, and then I read this travesty?? Eating Shredded Wheat is a more exciting experience than reading this, a reality which is even more shocking considering how excited I was to start this book. <br/><br/>I absolutely loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_' title='The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of Attolia</a>, but unfortunately this instalment had none of its predecessor’s charm. It wasn’t even that similar to the first of the series which at least merited a more solid three stars.</span>
  <span id="freeText11553174326446101547" style="display:none"><b>2.5 STARS</b><br /><br />What the hell happened here? This was supposed to become one of my favourite series, and then I read this travesty?? Eating Shredded Wheat is a more exciting experience than reading this, a reality which is even more shocking considering how excited I was to start this book. <br /><br />I absolutely loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a>, but unfortunately this instalment had none of its predecessor’s charm. It wasn’t even that similar to the first of the series which at least merited a more solid three stars. There are some similarities between all three, namely they all involve an attempt at a clever plot accompanied by a shocking reveal at the end. The key word here is ‘attempt’. While the second book convincingly pulled off a tightly plotted story, this one most definitely did not. It’s something everyone is aware of when they start a long series; will all the books be able to maintain the same quality or will one full victim to the dreaded middle-book-filler-syndrome? If I was aware of how much this series would fluctuate in quality from the start, I don’t think I would have bothered giving it the time of day at all. <br /><br />On to the main man of the series, Eugenides. So this guy has always had an unrealistically high sense of perception about the other characters and an alarmingly accurate sense of foresight, you know, of the kind you only ever find in literary characters. However, this book took Gen’s omnipotence to whole new levels, to the extent that it just smacked of lazy writing. Indeed, his entire characterisation was insufferable in so many ways. All the traits that I had found so endearing in the previous novels were taken way too far in this one. This probably wasn’t helped by the fact that the story shifts from Gen’s perspective to the perspective of the most boring, unimportant soldier the author could have possibly come up with. It was like she was trying to bore me? The soldier literally has no personality but we are now forced to follow him around <i>all day. Every. Single. Day</i>. Even if my life depended on it, I still wouldn’t be able to recall this dude’s name. Not only was this incredibly boring, but it also meant that we didn’t get any scenes of Attolia and Gen alone and this is the one thing I was looking forward to most after the ending of book two. It was frustrating to say the least and made me want to demand my money back, having naturally assumed when I purchased this book that because the title was <b>The King of Attolia</b> it would be from the perspective of the King of Attolia. It should be renamed random solider number 5 you won’t give two shits about.<br /> <br />Despite being longer than the second book, this one covered a fraction of the plot so no wonder it was always a struggle to pick it back again. Ultimately, I felt as if nothing had really changed across the course of the novel. Attolia was in pretty much the same position at the start of the book as it was by the end, and this whole book felt <i>pointless</i>. The fact that I still gave this three stars is a testament to how much I admired the author’s plotting in the previous book, because, honestly, even three stars is erring on the generous here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11553174326446101547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27387769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27387769" />
    <a title="Melissa McShane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1329059-melissa-mcshane"><img alt="Melissa McShane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216147749p2/1329059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27387769?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa McShane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa McShane" href="/user/show/1329059-melissa-mcshane">Melissa McShane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=alternate-world">alternate-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27387769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6461121929519127489">I think, on re-reading, that this is my favorite of The Queen's Thief series, probably because it's the payoff from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_' title='The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of Attolia</a>. Told primarily from the viewpoint of Costis, a young officer in the Queen of Attolia's guard, it's a masterful use of the unreliable narrator to tell two stories at once--but only if you've read the other books first. I'm sure it would still be enjoyable read on its own, but...wow, so much would be missing. So if you haven't read the others, please do.<br/><br/>Costis i</span>
  <span id="freeText6461121929519127489" style="display:none">I think, on re-reading, that this is my favorite of The Queen's Thief series, probably because it's the payoff from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a>. Told primarily from the viewpoint of Costis, a young officer in the Queen of Attolia's guard, it's a masterful use of the unreliable narrator to tell two stories at once--but only if you've read the other books first. I'm sure it would still be enjoyable read on its own, but...wow, so much would be missing. So if you haven't read the others, please do.<br /><br />Costis is a delight. He loves his Queen and is disdainful of the foppish, goat-footed Eddis boy (I still have no idea how old Eugenides is) who's forced himself upon her. But he's also honorable, which makes him a perfect POV character for this story. His observations of Eugenides are accurate and also completely wrong, as the reader knows but Costis does not. I loved seeing Gen through his eyes, knowing that Gen was playing the entire court of Attolia and wondering desperately what his game was and why he had to conceal himself. I also loved seeing him grow attached to Gen, who has a remarkable knack for making people love him.<br /><br />Eugenides, on the other hand, is never not amazing. One of my favorite throwaway scenes is when Costis reflects on the new king's quarters being where everyone would see him going to visit the queen at night BWAHAHAHAHA. He's clearly up to something, and we get hints of it, but I'm not ashamed to admit I didn't figure it out until it was revealed, because Gen is smarter than I am.<br /><br />I also love the way Gen and Irene's marriage is revealed through other people's observations. <i>We</i> know they love each other, but they're keeping that secret as part of Gen's plan, but there are moments, like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Gen is injured by assassins and Irene faints at the sight of his blood, and he nearly tears himself apart trying to reach her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when he's had another nightmare about being tortured by her and begs her to promise she won't do it, and her reassurance is so sweet and tender <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It makes their relationship even more compelling than if we'd had it from either of their perspectives.<br /><br />Aside from Eugenides' stated purpose for fooling the entire Attolian court, there's a second story going on here: Irene has made him her King, actual ruler over Attolia in her place, and Gen won't rise to the challenge. It becomes clear that this is the actual story when the first one is resolved and there's still a good 20% of the book left. Gen's resistance is rooted in a lot of personal issues, and without getting into more spoilers, I can say that resolving those makes for a powerful ending. This is one of those books that resonates with me for days after I finish reading it, and it is definitely one of my favorites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6461121929519127489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
